<div

col-a-2">













<div
class="header
artist_info_header
int-1
clearfix">














<h1
class="hed-1"
title="Bone
Thugs-N-Harmony"
itemprop="name">Bone
Thugs-N-Harmony</h1>














<div
class="header_btns">















<div
class="bookmark"
data-musicid="R82559"></div>














</div>













</div>













<div
class="int-1">














<div
class="content_right">















<div
class="artist_bio_container
clearfix">
















<div
class="artist_bio
short_bio">
















<div
class="artist_bio_inner">

















Graced
with
a
quick
and
sometimes
sung
delivery,
along
with
a
unique
sense
of
melody,
Bone
Thugs-N-Harmony
burst
out
of
Cleveland,
Ohio
in
the
mid-'90s
with
a
pair
of
massive
hits
(&quot;Thuggish
Ruggish
Bone&quot;
and
&quot;Tha
Crossroads&quot;)
along
with
a
great
first
album,
as
well
as
a
successful
follow-up,
and
then
quickly
unraveled.
Mainstream
interest
dropped
off
toward
the
tail
end
of
the
'90s,
but
the
group,
which
underwent
a
series
of
lineup
changes,
continued
to
release
new
material
via
mixtapes
and
albums
throughout
the
2000s.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>


















<a
href="/nwa"
class="hash">N.W.A</a>'s


















<a
href="/eazy-e"
class="hash">Eazy-E</a>
signed
the
group
--
initially
comprised
of


















<a
href="/krayzie-bone"
class="hash">Krayzie
Bone</a>,
Wish
Bone,
Flesh-N-Bone,


















<a
href="/layzie-bone-young-noble"
class="hash">Layzie
Bone</a>,
and


















<a
href="/bizzy-bone"
class="hash">Bizzy
Bone</a>
--
to
Ruthless
Records.
The
debut
release
from
Bone
was
an
EP,


















<a
href="#"
class="hash">Creepin
on
ah
Come
Up</a>
(1994).
The
EP
boasted
&quot;Thuggish
Ruggish
Bone,&quot;
a
conventional
G-funk
song
with
an
unconventional
array
of
Bone
Thug
rappers
that
became
an
overnight
summer
anthem,
especially
throughout
the
Midwest.
The
single
crossed
into
the
Billboard
Hot
100,
where
it
peaked
at
number
22.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Amid
the
fervor,
the
group
immediately
reentered
the
studio
and
emerged
with
a
remarkable
album,


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/e-1999-eternal-explicit"
class="hash">E
1999
Eternal</a>
(1995).
The
album
topped
the
Billboard
200
and
the
Top
R&amp;B/Hip-Hop
Albums
charts
and
spawned
a
pair
of
popular
singles,
&quot;1st
of
the
Month&quot;
and
&quot;Tha
Crossroads,&quot;
the
latter
a
dedication
to
the
deceased


















<a
href="/eazy-e"
class="hash">Eazy-E</a>
and
a
Grammy
Award
recipient.
As
was
in
vogue
at
the
time,
the
group
members
subsequently
pursued
respective
solo
careers
and
also
a
Mo
Thugs
Family
spinoff
group;
none
of
these
ventures
rivaled
the
proper
Bone
projects.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
At
this
point,
the
onetime
cohesive
group,
which
specialized
in
interwoven,
harmonious
singing
as
well
as
rapping,
became
conflicted
and
the
group
members
failed
to
collaborate
well.
However,
their
second
album,


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/art-of-war-explicit"
class="hash">Art
of
War</a>
(1997)
--
an
ambitious
double-disc
package
--
was
very
successful.
Not
only
did
it
top
the
same
Billboard
charts
as


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/e-1999-eternal-explicit"
class="hash">E
1999
Eternal</a>,
but
lead
single
&quot;Look
into
My
Eyes&quot;
went
Top
Five
on
the
Hot
100.
Within
a
year
of
release,
it
was
certified
quadruple
platinum
for
over
four
million
units
sold
in
the
U.S.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
A
second
round
of
solo
albums
sold
poorly,
and
Bone
quickly
slid
off
the
mainstream
radar.
Occasional
reunions,
such
as
2000's


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/btnhresurrection-explicit"
class="hash">BTNHResurrection</a>
and
2002's


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/thug-world-order-explicit"
class="hash">Thug
World
Order</a>,
produced
some
moments
of
glory,
but
these
were
few
and
far
between.
Thug
Stories,
released
in
2006
on
Koch,
placed
the
group
--
at
the
time,
a
trio
minus


















<a
href="/bizzy-bone"
class="hash">Bizzy</a>
--
in
the
Top
30
of
the
Billboard
200.
Bone
then
signed
to


















<a
href="/swizz-beatz"
class="hash">Swizz
Beatz</a>'s
Interscope-affiliated
Full
Surface
boutique
label,
where
they
issued
2007's


















<a
href="#"
class="hash">Strength
&amp;
Loyalty</a>.
A
major-label
budget
allowed
for
guest
spots
from


















<a
href="/game"
class="hash">the
Game</a>,


















<a
href="/mariah-carey"
class="hash">Mariah
Carey</a>,


















<a
href="/akon"
class="hash">Akon</a>,


















<a
href="/lil-bow-wow"
class="hash">Bow
Wow</a>,
and


















<a
href="/twista"
class="hash">Twista</a>,
and
the
set
eventually
sold
over
500,000
copies,
earning
gold
certification.


















<a
href="/bizzy-bone"
class="hash">Bizzy</a>
returned
for
2010's


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/uni-5-worlds-enemy-explicit"
class="hash">Uni5:
The
World's
Enemy</a>.
The
album
debuted
at
number
14
on
the
Billboard
200.
A
handful
of
dates
excepted,


















<a
href="/bizzy-bone"
class="hash">Bizzy</a>
was
absent
from
the
album's
promotional
tour.
He
returned
for
the
2013
release


















<a
href="/bone-thugs-n-harmony/art-of-war-wwiii-explicit"
class="hash">Art
of
War:
WWIII</a>,
but
this
time


















<a
href="/krayzie-bone"
class="hash">Krayzie</a>
and
Wish
Bone
were
out
of
the
group,
with
both
working
on
solo
careers.
~
Jason
Birchmeier,
Rovi
















</div>















</div>
















<a
href="#"
class="full_bio_link">full
bio</a>















</div>

read
this
because
it
actually
works.

will

on

Friday
by
the
love
of
your
life.

will
be
the
best
day
of
your
life.

if
you
don't
post
this
you
will
die
in
2
days.

you
started
reading
this
so
don't
stop.

is
so
scary

this
on
at
least
5
songs
in
the
next
143
minutes.

done

f6
and
your
lovers

will
appear
on
the
screen
in
big
letters
this
is
so
scary

}
